<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7635e1a7-43dc-4b5d-b833-3253e761e48b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText384958777279761040" style="display:none"><b>Destined for greatness . . .</b><br /><br />Four Clans of wild cats have shared the forest for generations, thriving in their territories. But tensions are running high, and ThunderClan must assert its strength or risk falling prey to its power-hungry neighbors.<br /><br />Into this time of uncertainty, a kit is born. A prophecy foretells that Bluekit will be as strong as fire, destined to blaze through the ranks of her Clan. But with this prophecy comes the foreshadowing of her destruction by the one enemy she cannot outrun.<br /><br />As Bluekit gains power and eventually earns her leader name, Bluestar, she fights to protect her Clan. But secrets from the past threaten to surface--secrets that may destroy ThunderClan . . . and Bluestar.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_461122619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461122619" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5077124-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326849368p2/5077124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/461122619?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/5077124-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461122619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer684653429401510212">I bought this book when I was twelve. Now, as I am rapidly approaching sixteen, you'd think I would've at least FORCED myself to grow out of the Warriors series, to prove that "IMMA GROWNUP MOMMY!!!"<br/><br/>But no.<br/><br/>They're amazing, I reread them constantly, and if you don't like it then bite me.<br/><br/>Anyway.<br/><br/>This book starts the day Bluekit opens her eyes for the first time, and follows her as she grows into Bluefur, a fierce Thunderclan warrior haunted by the death of her loved ones and the hostility of her bl</span>
  <span id="freeText684653429401510212" style="display:none">I bought this book when I was twelve. Now, as I am rapidly approaching sixteen, you'd think I would've at least FORCED myself to grow out of the Warriors series, to prove that "IMMA GROWNUP MOMMY!!!"<br /><br />But no.<br /><br />They're amazing, I reread them constantly, and if you don't like it then bite me.<br /><br />Anyway.<br /><br />This book starts the day Bluekit opens her eyes for the first time, and follows her as she grows into Bluefur, a fierce Thunderclan warrior haunted by the death of her loved ones and the hostility of her bloodthirsty Clanmate, Thistleclaw.<br /><br />I... I... Oh God I just can't. I can't revisit it, not again. I still haven't recovered. You'd think that after the sixth read, I would be better prepared for the horrible tragedy and emotions of the stupid book. But no. I still bawl my eyes out. EVERY FU.... FREAKING TIME.<br /><br />This is the only book that has ever EVER made me cry. EVER. And I read a ton. The last fifth or so of the book is like the ending of Marley &amp; Me. It will scar you for life, but the pain is so sweet that you constantly crawl back, ripping deeper scars into your soul with every visit.<br /><br />I have discovered that crying over a book is one of the best, most humiliating feelings in the world. Especially if you're weeping over the angst of a moody cat. Jesus. I need a social life.<br /><br />Anywho, just to make myself clear: This is the best Warriors book ever written. It has the magic of the original (aka BEST) six books, the writing finesse of the later books, and the strength of character that can only be reached by digging into the innermost workings of a beloved character's soul. To have experienced Bluestar's ENTIRE LIFE is amazing. I've never had that deep of an experience with a character. You can see the threads connecting every moment of her life and how they affected her in the post-Fireheart novels. I loved it with every fiber of my lonely emo being, and will probably reread it countless times more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="684653429401510212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11692465285364630975">This is probably my second favorite super edition, second to Crookedstar's Promise. I really enjoyed Bluestar's prophecy. You enter the story moments before Bluestar jumps off the edge of the gorge to lead the dogs to their deaths, but this time from her perspective. The prophecy, (which she refer's to as Goosefeather's) rings in her mind. <i> Water will destroy you...</i> It ends with Mistyfoot and Stonefur forgiving her for what she's done.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed the elements and setup of this book. It flas</span>
  <span id="freeText11692465285364630975" style="display:none">This is probably my second favorite super edition, second to Crookedstar's Promise. I really enjoyed Bluestar's prophecy. You enter the story moments before Bluestar jumps off the edge of the gorge to lead the dogs to their deaths, but this time from her perspective. The prophecy, (which she refer's to as Goosefeather's) rings in her mind. <i> Water will destroy you...</i> It ends with Mistyfoot and Stonefur forgiving her for what she's done.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the elements and setup of this book. It flashes into Bluestar's life from kit to leader, and all the tragedy and heartbreak she went through. Seeing as I got my copy at a used book sale, it's pretty beat up, but every time I pick it up I just get this wonderful nostalgic feeling. If you feel nostalgic when looking at Into the Wild after reading the newest book, it's multiplied with this one.<br />The feels are real. Would recommend!</span>

<div id="review_1630843837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630843837" />
    <a title="Liam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54212000-liam"><img alt="Liam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492710778p2/54212000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630843837?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam" href="/user/show/54212000-liam">Liam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061582509" href="/book/show/6798773-bluestar-s-prophecy">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">diehard Warriors fans only</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Liam by: </span>
      Sister
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=blibbering-humdingers-are-missing">blibbering-humdingers-are-missing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=bad">bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=failed">failed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=avoid-at-all-costs">avoid-at-all-costs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54212000-liam?shelf=mixed-emotions">mixed-emotions</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630843837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18174997985396121602">Okay, I have to admit. I like the idea. I like going back to see what happened with Bluestar before Firepaw came in. I also have to admit something else. I didn't like this book.<br/><br/>Bluestar was just annoying. Her decisions made no sense. I didn't get her at all. Oakheart was, eh, dumb. I totally think Crookedpaw was nicer. Side note: I loved Crookedpaw's character. I absolutely love his loyalty. He is overly friendly at gatherings, but in battle, he's fiercely loyal to his clan, which I appreciate.</span>
  <span id="freeText18174997985396121602" style="display:none">Okay, I have to admit. I like the idea. I like going back to see what happened with Bluestar before Firepaw came in. I also have to admit something else. I didn't like this book.<br /><br />Bluestar was just annoying. Her decisions made no sense. I didn't get her at all. Oakheart was, eh, dumb. I totally think Crookedpaw was nicer. Side note: I loved Crookedpaw's character. I absolutely love his loyalty. He is overly friendly at gatherings, but in battle, he's fiercely loyal to his clan, which I appreciate.<br /><br />Okay, back on track. Yes, Sunfall/star was actually pretty good. Pinestar was, uh, okay. Kinda stupid, but okay. Thistleclaw was actually pretty cool, even if he was evil. Thrushpelt.... oh, Thrushpelt, I pity you :) He reminds me of Peeta, a little bit. Big softie. Very down to earth. Unfortunately for him, his Katniss (Kat-niss?) didn't like him back. Oh well, I think he probably got over her. Actually, wait, no, I don't think he did -_- wow. Never mind. Anyway.... who am I forgetting? Oh, yeah, Snowfur. Poor her. I don't know. She was kind of annoying, and I don't get what she saw in Thistleclaw (hey, me and Bluefur agree on something!).<br /><br />Apart from the characters, this book was absolute crap (some of the characters were crap too, or else it might have gotten 3 stars). The plot was pointless. It's because of these books that I've come to hate prophesies in books with a vengeance. Goosebutt, or whatever his name was (Gooseflower? No. Goosepelt? No. Goosejerk? Yes, that's more like it), was perhaps the most annoying character ever. Worst pick for medicine cat, I admit. Wait, I'm going on about the characters. Never mind. Alright, the plot. Too many prophesies in the Warriors books. I know they're supposed to be important, but I just hate them. The story in this book felt like it was just being dragged out. Some scenes felt important to the plot, but (as is typical with these books) there were just SO many pointless scenes that drove me insane. I really have no sympathy for Bluefur, despite all she went through. I don't know. Maybe it was because she actually wasn't that nice at times, and way too ambitious. I like an unambitious lead, but she was the opposite.<br /><br />Okay, I'll conclude this. Basically, I hated this book. It was the worst, probably, of the Special Editions, at least the ones I've read, and I don't have any particular sympathy for Bluestar after reading it. I thought maybe we'd get to see why she had doubts about the loyalty of her own clan, but no, we didn't. I thought we'd get a better story. But it was pretty bad.<br /><br />The only part I liked was the little epilogue, with Spottedleaf and Bluestar, and Rusty, and the whole 'get Graypaw to track him' thing. By the way, why in later books are apprentices not even really allowed out alone, but in this one they're being sent on missions next to Twoleg-place, or whatever they called it?<br /><br />All in all, just awful -_-<br /><br />(Also, Bluefur and Oakheart had a damn one night stand. Really!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18174997985396121602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7899506785718843899" style="display:none">Wow! I LOVED this book! IT WAS AMAZING! My favourite ever book! I've read it again a few times and enjoyed it loads. <span id="freeTextContainer5921753214485843691">This was an excellent book! I liked it even better that Firestar's Quest.<br/><br/> This book starts out when the famous Bluestar was just a kit. This book travels through her life from kit to leader. Bluestar is given a prophecy, and with it death, lies and heartache await. Bluestar has endured them all. So when she is told by Starclan to give up her kits to save Thunderclan, Bluestar makes a heart throbbing decision. What will it be? Well... read the book and find out.<br/><br/>(Revised 6-8-11)</span>

<div id="review_184279433" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184279433" />
    <a title="Kay Causer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5281616-kay-causer"><img alt="Kay Causer" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184279433?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kay Causer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kay Causer" href="/user/show/5281616-kay-causer">Kay Causer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5281616-kay-causer?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer184279433&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184279433" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17715862540261921953">So, this is my first Goodreads review. Hope it goes well *fingers crossed*<br/><br/>I read the original Warriors series over a number of years (the books were very hard to find in the UK) and then always meant to go back and read the New Prophecy series (I have the whole box set on order right now). But then I heard about the Super Editions. Having only read the original series they sounded great. New books that I didn't need to read all of New Prophecy to understand. Of course I went for Bluestar's first</span>
  <span id="freeText17715862540261921953" style="display:none">So, this is my first Goodreads review. Hope it goes well *fingers crossed*<br /><br />I read the original Warriors series over a number of years (the books were very hard to find in the UK) and then always meant to go back and read the New Prophecy series (I have the whole box set on order right now). But then I heard about the Super Editions. Having only read the original series they sounded great. New books that I didn't need to read all of New Prophecy to understand. Of course I went for Bluestar's first.<br /><br />Now, I must say I am way over the age meant for these books. I started reading them in my late teens because they seemed like something I would have adored as a kid. I couldn't help myself. A series about cats that's full og mysticism but also the brutal reality of nature. Even as an adult I can't help myself and I've never much cared for only reading things because of the age put on it.<br /><br />Enough background. I got Bluestar's Prophecy and raced through it. There was good and bad, it must be said but as a companion to the original series I don't think fans will be disappointed.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />First the bad. Let's get it out the way. <br />I had assumed that there'd be a lot more about Bluestar and Oakheart's relationship. It was really based on nothing more than attraction and one careless night spent together. I supose that made more sense in a way. Bluestar was too loyal to do what Greystripe/Silverstream did, seeing each other repeatedly. It made more sense that she snuck out one night because she was young, curious and caught up in the moment.<br /><br />Another problem I had was with how Bluestar was chosen to be deputy. She seemed too young and like she hadn't done anything special to earn the title. I get that Sunstar wanted a young deputy who he could mold into the future leader he wanted but that should have been made clearer by him talking to her and Thistleclaw about it imo.<br /><br />Her decision to give up her kits seemed a bit out of the blue too. There should have been more build up, more or her worrying over her decision, more of Thistleclaw being bloodthirsty to push her to do it. Given the fact she had no interest in kits before hers were born it didn't paint her in a very good light that she gave them up so easily.<br /><br />However, there were a lot of good (and great) things about the book which is why I gave it 4 stars.<br /><br />I loved seeing all the Warriors characters when they were younger. Some of the new characters were great too. I loved Sunfall/star, Pinestar, young Crookedstar when he was still friendly and playful, Snowfur, little Whitestorm, Featherwhisker and poor Thrushpelt. Bluestar could have been nicer to him. I really wanted someone to appreciate how sweet and loving he was.<br /><br />Tigerstar made a lot more sense too after reading the book. Thistleclaw instilled a lot of bloodlust in him - the way he made him attack the little black kit was one of the most powerful scenes in the book, especially when you know who that kit grew up to be. The fact that he was so spoilt as the only kit in the clan also shows some of his arrogance. It was probably always in his personality to be as power hungry and ruthless as he became but other events in Bluestar's Prophecy show how this personality was encouraged. He even hates kittypets so much because his father abandoned the clan to live a kittypet life.<br /><br />The most revealing thing in the book to me, however, was Bluestar's depression everytime she lost someone. It made her severe depression after Tigerstar's betrayal make much more sense. When her mother died she barely functioned for months until Sunfall talked her out of it. The same thing happened again when Snowfur died and she later gave up her kits. Everytime she withdrew from clan life as much as she could and had few close bonds with the other cats. The only cat who could talk her around was Sunstar but by the time Tigerclaw betrayed her he wasn't around. As clan leader she was even more disconnected from the clan when she went into depression.<br /><br />In short, I liked this book and all it revealed. Of course, I do think it helps to have read the Warriors series to get the most out of it. In fact, until I read Crookedstar's Promise I still probably won't have the full picture.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17715862540261921953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1278390872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278390872" />
    <a title="Nicoledp67" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6252992-nicoledp67"><img alt="Nicoledp67" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316039707p2/6252992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1278390872?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicoledp67" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicoledp67" href="/user/show/6252992-nicoledp67">Nicoledp67</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1278390872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13330573473262660697">I've had this book since I was eleven. I'm now seventeen and in the process of re-reading it for the millionth time. Do I care if I'm too old to still be reading this series? Oh look, there goes the mouse tails I give.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Bluestar's mother's death was the most heartbreaking scene in this book. Or, I should say, <i>one</i> of the most heartbreaking scenes in this book. I can't believe Hawkheart went on to join StarClan in the end, it's just as... well, unjustified as Ashfur's fate in the afte</span></span>
  <span id="freeText13330573473262660697" style="display:none">I've had this book since I was eleven. I'm now seventeen and in the process of re-reading it for the millionth time. Do I care if I'm too old to still be reading this series? Oh look, there goes the mouse tails I give.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bluestar's mother's death was the most heartbreaking scene in this book. Or, I should say, <i>one</i> of the most heartbreaking scenes in this book. I can't believe Hawkheart went on to join StarClan in the end, it's just as... well, unjustified as Ashfur's fate in the afterlife. His excuse was that he "loved too much," which is complete fox dung in my opinion. What was Hawkheart's excuse? That Moonflower was just following her leader's orders in destroying their medicine supply? Ugh, I will never get over that piece of fox dung. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Although some hardcore Warrior fans [such as myself] don't particularly agree with the choice of her mother's name, Moonflower, ("Moon" is hardly a name one would give to their kit, considering it belongs to the sacred Moonstone and Moonpool) it's pretty and convenient, so I'll let that slide.<br /><br />...Sunstar, however...just no.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The second most heartbreaking scene on the list is Snowfur's death. The way Bluefur had to break it to her son, Whitekit, was just... I can't even describe the pain I felt for Whitekit and Bluefur, the bearer of bad news. Everyone gives Bluefur a hard time for how she dealt with Moonflower's death as well as that of her sister's, but honestly, I wouldn't be coping much better in her shoes... I mean her paws.<br /><br />Five years after I first read this book, I didn't have a clue why Snowfur's first catch had its fur parted in an ominous way. But now I realize it was a sign from StarClan foretelling her death, and the path that would lead away from her sister's - she would be a mother whose life ended too soon, and Bluepaw, who was the first of the two to catch this really large squirrel, would be ThunderClan's future leader.<br /><br />I see what you did there, Erins. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I loved all the names in this book. They were simple and yet telling, not too fancy or flashy like some of the Omen of the Stars cats.<br /><br />For example: Larksong the elder, the two Queens Swiftbreeze and Poppydawn, Pinestar's mother- the deceased Sweetbriar, Dawnstripe, Reedfeather and Fallowtail from WindClan, Littlebird (my personal favorite out of all the names in this book), and Hollyflower from ShadowClan, and I think there are some more but these are all the names I could recall off the top of my head w/o using the book.<br /><br />If you're hesitating in buying the book just because it's labeled for children, just go for it and buy the book -- it won't hurt. (Much.) In my opinion, this book doesn't have the soft barrier other children novels do, and therefore its incorrect in the categorization of a children's book.<br /><br />It was a great book the first time I read it in 2009, when it first released, and it's <b>still</b> a great book <i>five years later</i>.<br /><br />Seriously, take my word for it. You won't regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13330573473262660697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It reveals so many secrets from the normal series that I've been dying to know about since the very first book of, like, a twenty book series.   <span id="freeText16237618805747578577" style="display:none">I LOVED THIS BOOK. It reveals so many secrets from the normal series that I've been dying to know about since the very first book of, like, a twenty book series. I love the way Erin Hunter describes the way the cats think. It's so descriptive, and it seems to describe the exact opposite of the way that people think cats think. Bluestar is an amazing she-cat, and she is beautiful and brilliant as leader to ThunderClan, for many moons. At least that's what everyone thinks. She has so many secrets yet for her clan to discover, and some which they will never discover. That she had kits, Mistyfoot and her brother, Stonefur. That she loved Oakheart. That she never believed that Tigerstar was really an enemy to fear until he tried to kill her. She hated herself and was disgusted at herself for it, so that she risked her life for Fireheart, knowing she wouldn't survive. It's an amazing book, and it starts from when she was born. I recommend it to anyone who loves cats, or even hates cats. It's an amazing, suspenseful book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8090554613524193043">Anyone even remotely familiar with Erin Hunter's "Warriors" series knows of Bluestar, the great cat who preceeded Firestar in leading ThunderClan. But most probably don't know of the struggles she went through, the losses she endured, and the decisions she had to make on while on her rise to power. Also hints at why Tigerclaw became so vicious and how ThunderClan cats earned the reputation as kitty pet sympathizers even before Firetar became a 'paw'.<br/><br/>"Bluestar's Prophecy" reads almost like a biog</span>
  <span id="freeText8090554613524193043" style="display:none">Anyone even remotely familiar with Erin Hunter's "Warriors" series knows of Bluestar, the great cat who preceeded Firestar in leading ThunderClan. But most probably don't know of the struggles she went through, the losses she endured, and the decisions she had to make on while on her rise to power. Also hints at why Tigerclaw became so vicious and how ThunderClan cats earned the reputation as kitty pet sympathizers even before Firetar became a 'paw'.<br /><br />"Bluestar's Prophecy" reads almost like a biography of this great feline leader, detailing her life from birth to taking over leadership of her Clan. Has everything: Drama, suspense, romance, secrets, lies, intrigue, a few shock moments...and, of course, the legendary battle scenes Warriors fans have come to expect. Can stand alone or act as a prequel to the "Into the Wild." <br /><br />A great book, as I have come to expect from the writers of this series. </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3197616862792784341" style="display:none">In the beginning I was really confused. It started out with Bluestar dieing and then she was in the nursery as a kit. But just the page before she was an old she cat who was dead. Was she remembering her life or or was it starclan giving her a chance to relive her life. To make sure she didn't make the mistake of Tigerstar again.<br /><br />If everybody got a second chance at life then life would have no meaning. That's why you have to always try your hardest. You get one chance. One shot. And you can't do it over. if everybody got a second chance then people wouldn't try. The world would be in a mess. So many people would be suffering because of the dumb choices they made because they knew <br />they had a second chance.<br /><br />That's why i think bluestars prophecy wasn't about her getting a second chance. And it also wasn't a memory. But at the same time it was a memory. It was her reliving her life but not in a second chance kind of way. It was also not in a narrative way. It was just her whole life story from her point of view. Like she is telling us what made her the way she is in the first 5 books. For example when she turns her back to starclan. That wasn't just from out of the blue. It was because so many terrible things had happened in her life. Losing her mother then her sister. Then having her most senior warrior betray her in the most brutal way. she just snapped. It was to much for her. And it left her torn in 2. <br /> </span>

  <span id="freeText5618044494567402185" style="display:none">Everyone knows Bluestar from the first book of the first series of Warriors to the second last book, right? No. <br /><br />More questions were asked about Bluestar's past until FINALLY Erin Hunter opened up and released 'Bluestar's Prophecy', as this review is about.<br /><br />The story takes place in ThunderClan and two young kits that were born were about to change ThunderClan's world...forever.<br /><br />Bluekit and Snowkit are two seemingly ordinary kits that love to play around and have fun until the old medicine cat, Goosefeather comes up to Bluekit and tells her...<br /><br /><i>Like fire, you will blaze through the forest, but beware, even the strongest flames can be drenched by water...</i><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[That is rather ironic, considering that Bluestar died drowning... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Soon Bluekit is Bluepaw to Bluefur, and more and more often, she is hit by wave after wave of loss, stress and bloodlust battling. More losses hit Bluefur in the heart than the body.<br /><br />Soon a secret romance with Oakheart interferes with Bluefur's life and soon, her destiny.<br /><br />And one more question to ask herself.<br /><br />Is she <b>really</b> the fire that will blaze through?<br /><br />All your questions about Bluestar<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and surprisingly enough, TIGERSTAR <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>are answered in 'Bluestar's Prophecy'<br /><br />May the stars light your way.</span>

<div id="review_227925176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227925176" />
    <a title="08emilyr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6252509-08emilyr"><img alt="08emilyr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325696374p2/6252509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227925176?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="08emilyr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="08emilyr" href="/user/show/6252509-08emilyr">08emilyr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227925176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5057510471784762922">Bluestar's Prophecy by Erin Hunter<br/><br/>Bluestar's prophecy is a special edition of the Warriors series. It takes place long before the chronological series, and tells the story of Bluestar, Thunderclan's leader, and her rise to the top. Bluestar is given a prophecy when she is young, foretelling that she wil be like fire, blazing through the ranks of her clan. At first, she feels that she'll always be an ordinary warrior, but her life turns lonely and heart breaking, as those around her begin to die,</span>
  <span id="freeText5057510471784762922" style="display:none">Bluestar's Prophecy by Erin Hunter<br /><br />Bluestar's prophecy is a special edition of the Warriors series. It takes place long before the chronological series, and tells the story of Bluestar, Thunderclan's leader, and her rise to the top. Bluestar is given a prophecy when she is young, foretelling that she wil be like fire, blazing through the ranks of her clan. At first, she feels that she'll always be an ordinary warrior, but her life turns lonely and heart breaking, as those around her begin to die, and she is forced to give up her three kits for the sake of her Clan. Bluestar's journey is a real tear-jerker, mixed in with plenty of action and stories of love, loss, and redemption.<br /><br />I rate this book: Four stars, because the storyline was excellent, and the characters were so intensely strong and loyal, that I found myself feeling just like them when I finished to book.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone who enjoys the Warriors series, and also to people who like to read about animals. This is a brilliant story told through the heart of a witty, wonderful cat. I would even say that ANYONE could delight in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5057510471784762922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_540730729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/540730729" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17624257-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455813520p2/17624257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/540730729?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/17624257-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17624257-cara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17624257-cara?shelf=warriors">warriors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540730729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13702546311727202403">I absolutely loved this book, which is one of my favorite Super Editions. I always liked Bluestar through the 1st Warriors series, so I snapped this book up. Well. This book gives all the details on Bluestar's life before the first book, and it's more of a narrative about Bluestar than just her short summary in Forest of Secrets.<br/><br/>I think one of the things I enjoyed most about this book was the detail on ThunderClan before Bluestar's leadership and seeing the connection between characters, such as</span>
  <span id="freeText13702546311727202403" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book, which is one of my favorite Super Editions. I always liked Bluestar through the 1st Warriors series, so I snapped this book up. Well. This book gives all the details on Bluestar's life before the first book, and it's more of a narrative about Bluestar than just her short summary in Forest of Secrets.<br /><br />I think one of the things I enjoyed most about this book was the detail on ThunderClan before Bluestar's leadership and seeing the connection between characters, such as Halftail, who was actually Bluestar's sister's mentor. I also loved seeing Bluestar grow, from an adventurous little kit to the strong and respected leader. I was fascinated by the little secrets and plot twists that grew into significant factors later on. And, of course, this Super Edition would not be complete without detailing her struggles with deputyship (is that a word?) and motherhood, all of which are provided and narrated emotionally. I was surprised in a good way at all of this-considering it was written after the entire first series, it tied in with what I already knew surprisingly well. So happy I bought a copy on my Kindle Fire so I can read it any time I want!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13702546311727202403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_392302597" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392302597" />
    <a title="Hails" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11892771-hails"><img alt="Hails" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345040291p2/11892771.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392302597?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hails" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hails" href="/user/show/11892771-hails">Hails</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392302597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2909474000004583886">This is by far the most spectacular book of the lengthy Warriors series. Bluestar is a beloved character, and we all know what she's been through. Until you read <i>Bluestar's Prophecy</i>, however, you can't even begin to appreciate just what makes this legendary she-cat so heroic. From losing her beloved family members one by one in death, to dealing with a forbidden love and making historic choices that shape her Clans future, Bluestar will prove to you once and for all that she always had her Clan'</span>
  <span id="freeText2909474000004583886" style="display:none">This is by far the most spectacular book of the lengthy Warriors series. Bluestar is a beloved character, and we all know what she's been through. Until you read <i>Bluestar's Prophecy</i>, however, you can't even begin to appreciate just what makes this legendary she-cat so heroic. From losing her beloved family members one by one in death, to dealing with a forbidden love and making historic choices that shape her Clans future, Bluestar will prove to you once and for all that she always had her Clan's best interests at heart; but living with a paw in two seperate worlds always leads to disaster...<br /><br />What I loved most about this special edition was the emotional depth and personifcation of Bluestar's character. For once we finally get to see stronger, deeper feelings of remorse over the loss of precious Clanmembers. Bluestar had a heart so big that she seemed far more human than cat; one can easily relate to her biased motivations and her anguished mental space. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2909474000004583886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2005679779?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ʟ ᴇ ᴀ ʜ ¯\_(ツ)_/¯" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ʟ ᴇ ᴀ ʜ ¯\_(ツ)_/¯" href="/user/show/54768100">ʟ ᴇ ᴀ ʜ ¯\_(ツ)_/¯</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005679779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9921181661552541534">SPOILERS AHEAD! If you haven't read the book and you don't want to get spoiled, I wouldn't suggest reading ahead. Don't say I didn't warn you.<br/><br/>The rants contained in this review are out-of-order. Each event happened in a different order in the book.<br/><br/>I had wanted to read this book for <i>such</i> a long time, but I was quite disappointed when I finally read it. I was hoping that this book would explain some of the occurrences of the first series, but it was only about Bluekit/Bluepaw/Bluefur/Bluestar's li</span>
  <span id="freeText9921181661552541534" style="display:none">SPOILERS AHEAD! If you haven't read the book and you don't want to get spoiled, I wouldn't suggest reading ahead. Don't say I didn't warn you.<br /><br />The rants contained in this review are out-of-order. Each event happened in a different order in the book.<br /><br />I had wanted to read this book for <i>such</i> a long time, but I was quite disappointed when I finally read it. I was hoping that this book would explain some of the occurrences of the first series, but it was only about Bluekit/Bluepaw/Bluefur/Bluestar's life. Growing up, completing her training, and becoming a warrior.<br />I don't get what Snowfur saw in Thistleclaw. He was a battle-blind idiot. ;-; I suppose Whitestorm made their relationship worth it.<br />Bluefur's attitude after her mother and Snowfur's deaths made me want to hide under a rock and die.<br />Bluefur didn't even have a legit relationship with Oakheart. They saw each other from their borders a few times, and they hung out for <i>one</i> night. Afterwards, they decided to end their "friendship", and avoid each other. Then <b>boom</b>, Bluefur's carrying Oakhearts kits. -_- Seriously?<br />I pitied Thrushpelt the entire time. He was mooning over Bluefur for so long, and she still chose a RiverClan tom over one from her own clan.<br />Pinestar left ThunderClan to become a kittypet... &gt;.&lt; <br />Snowfur's death was halfway interesting, but she was stupid to chase the ShadowClan invaders over the Thunderpath. Every cat knows that they're going to get run over if they try that, which is why they don't.<br />Goosefeather drove me insane. x_x Prophecy this, prophecy that.<br />Sunstar seemed like a decent cat, but I would've thought he was smarter than to choose Thistleclaw as Tigerpaw's mentor. '-' And I don't understand why Bluefur was appointed as deputy after Tawnyspots was no longer able. She has never proven her loyalty, and she hasn't done anything that suggests she should have been considered in the first place. 'Youth over experience' isn't good enough for me.<br />Bluefur had to get rid of her kits to become deputy, of course. She wouldn't have been appointed over Thistleclaw if she was a mother. But she shouldn't have had an interest in Oakheart at all. If she hadn't she wouldn't have had the kits. :P<br /><br />The best parts of this book were the prologue and ending.<br />It was interesting to see the wolf pack scene in Bluestar's POV. <br />And the ending, when Bluestar saw Rusty for the first time and ordered Graypaw to keep an eye near the fence, was very intriguing. I had always wanted to know why Graypaw was out alone when he attacked Rusty in book one (Even though it still doesn't make sense; apprentices aren't allowed to roam the territory by themselves.).<br /><br />Ta-daaa. My review. :P I wish I could rate this book five stars, but it wasn't worth that rating in my opinion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9921181661552541534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18010439368198318080">This explains so many things. And it makes me love Bluestar even more than I already did.<br/>It's an intense character on Bluestar and her life before we meet her in Into the Wild.<br/>It's especially funny when you recognize all the old characters and see them grow up (Lionpaw, I mean you especially).<br/>We see so much of Bluestar's character growth and the choices that shaped her life. And it shows her struggles with StarClan and her own choices. Her love story is only a small part of her arc and I enjoyed</span>
  <span id="freeText18010439368198318080" style="display:none">This explains so many things. And it makes me love Bluestar even more than I already did.<br />It's an intense character on Bluestar and her life before we meet her in Into the Wild.<br />It's especially funny when you recognize all the old characters and see them grow up (Lionpaw, I mean you especially).<br />We see so much of Bluestar's character growth and the choices that shaped her life. And it shows her struggles with StarClan and her own choices. Her love story is only a small part of her arc and I enjoyed that very much.<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I have so many thoughts and feelings about this.<br />- Snowfur and Bluestar share such a special relationship. I loved to see them grow apart and not knowing exactly how to find back.<br />- her distant das made me so mad<br />- The friendship between Crookedpaw and Bluepaw was adorable and I would have loved to see more of those two<br />- Moonflowers death killed me. I knew she was gonna die early in the book but I didn't realize Bluepaw saw it happen ;___;<br />- Sunfall is such a good mentor and strong character. He held the Clan together when they felt devastated after Pinestar left<br />- That whole thing was so well fore-shadowed btw, well done. <br />- And Jake! Firestar's dad! I cannot believe!<br />- small Tigerclaw was interesting to see. I was not fond of him in the first series but I do feel I understand him better now<br />- Oh, Bluestar's hate for Yellowfang makes so much more sense now! It's so obvious when you know the facts<br />- Goosefeather confused me a bit, I felt bad for all the flak he got from his Clanmates<br />- Featherwhisker was such a sweetheart; no wonder Spottedleaf turned out so great. Loved his humour<br />- Whitefur named after his mom? My poor heart<br />- Thrushpelt, my poor boy! Most loyal of all, I am so sad he never got to raise (his own) kits. He reminds me of Grey Wing in a way that hurts<br />- now to the hardest part: Oakheart. Geez. First of all, why did we not see him in his full pining glory? I feel robbed. His every interaction with Bluepelt was soft and sweet and broke me. <br />- Bluepelt deciding between her Clan or her kits? StarClan is truly cruel.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <span id="freeText16342093677382918139" style="display:none">My other BFF let me borrow this book from her, so TY BFF.<br />Bluestars prophecy, I rated this book 5/5, it was a great read!<br />This book is about a young cat, who started off being known as Bluekit, and basically as in the title states, is her life in ThunderCan.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LMeESUiTjF0GgHvbyeo5G/emEXawgeu25S89xcj7hw8IrUuMUfI7Fs1RBDG2gfkr9zuZpALmVAm0OLyyQ1rnfg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P8ArCPD1up9iFRPr27VEayVGnlk/WMQnP+hxVf3Qqm0bquTN6ZQN1KnEbAGk3oRbJdsWi40/e5hu//AidnHKHA==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText11796000471558917136" style="display:none">Erin Hunter is the pseudonym of five people: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/132369.Kate_Cary" title="Kate Cary" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Cary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220345.Cherith_Baldry" title="Cherith Baldry" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherith Baldry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/374504.Tui_T__Sutherland" title="Tui T. Sutherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Tui T. Sutherland</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2742182.Gillian_Philip" title="Gillian Philip" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Philip</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/769868.Inbali_Iserles" title="Inbali Iserles" rel="nofollow noopener">Inbali Iserles</a>, as well as editor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/645010.Victoria_Holmes" title="Victoria Holmes" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holmes</a>. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
